                    https://www.johndcook.com/unicode_latex.html  #=Unicode Code Point to Latex Converter

                    https://www.unicode.org/charts/PDF/U2200.pdf

                    This page lists the characters in the Mathematical Operators block of the Unicode standard (version 16.0), which covers 256 code points from U+2200 to U+22FF, all of which have been assigned.
                    All characters in this block have the General_Category value Sm (Math_Symbol) and the Script value Zyyy (Common).
                    Code point 	Image
                    edit 	Character 	Name
                                blank-tab-tab
                                    |     tab
                                    |      |

            Notes
            To get a list of code charts for a character, enter its code in the search box at the top. To access a chart for a given block, click on its entry in the table. The charts are PDF files, and some of them may be very large. For frequent access to the same chart, right-click and save the file to your disk. For an alphabetical index of character and block names, use the Unicode Character Names Index.

        Notes

            1.^ As of Unicode version 15.0
            2.^ Grey areas indicate non-assigned code points

        Note I: The ligatures ◊∞ ◊± ◊≤‚Äé are intended for Yiddish. They are not used in Hebrew.
        Note II: The symbol ◊¥‚Äé is called gershayim and is a punctuation mark used in the Hebrew language to denote acronyms. It is written before the last letter in the acronym. Gershayim is also the name of a note of cantillation in the reading of the Torah, printed above the accented letter.

        Remaining graphs are in the Alphabetic Presentation Forms block:

        Note: In Yiddish orthography only, the glyph, yud-·∏•iriq (Ô¨ù‚Äé), pronounced /i/, can be optionally used, rather than typing yud then ·∏•iriq (◊ô÷¥‚Äé). In Hebrew spelling this would be pronounced /ji/.  /i/ is written ·∏•iriq under the previous letter then yud ( ÷¥ ◊ô‚Äé).
        HTML code tables

        Note: HTML numeric character references can be in decimal format (&#DDDD;) or hexadecimal format (&#xHHHH;). For example, &#1490; and &#x05D2; (where "05D2" in hexadecimal is the same as "1490" in decimal) both represent the Hebrew letter gimmel.

'cyrillic supplement'  #abkhaz, kurdish, azeri (etc)
        https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyrillic_Supplement
        Cyrillic Supplement is a Unicode block containing Cyrillic letters for writing several minority languages, including Abkhaz, Kurdish, Komi, Mordvin, Aleut, Azerbaijani, and Jakovlev's Chuvash orthography.
        Block
        Cyrillic Supplement[1]

        Blocks
        Main articles: Cherokee (Unicode block) and Cherokee Supplement

        The main Unicode block for Cherokee is U+13A0‚ÄìU+13FF.[d] It contains the script's upper-case syllables as well as six lower-case syllables.

        A single Cherokee Unicode font, Plantagenet Cherokee, is supplied with macOS, version 10.3 (Panther) and later. Windows Vista also includes a Cherokee font. Several free Cherokee fonts are available including Digohweli, Donisiladv, and Noto Sans Cherokee. Some pan-Unicode fonts, such as Code2000, Everson Mono, and GNU FreeFont, include Cherokee characters. A commercial font, Phoreus Cherokee, published by TypeCulture, includes multiple weights and styles.[89] The Cherokee Nation Language Technology Program supports "innovative solutions for the Cherokee language on all digital platforms including smartphones, laptops, desktops, tablets and social networks."[90]
        Vocabulary
        Cherokee stop sign, Tahlequah, Oklahoma, with ·é†·é¥·è´·èç·èó·é≠ "alehwisdiha" (also spelled "halehwisda") meaning 'stop'
        Cherokee traffic sign in Tahlequah, Oklahoma, reading ·èù ·é†·èó ·è±·é© "tla adi yigi", meaning 'no parking' from "tla" meaning 'no'
        Numbers

        Cherokee uses Arabic numerals (0‚Äì9). The Cherokee council voted not to adopt Sequoyah's numbering system.[91] Sequoyah created individual symbols for 1‚Äì20, 30, 40, 50, 60, 70, 80, 90, and 100 as well as a symbol for three zeros for numbers in the thousands, and a symbol for six zeros for numbers in the millions. These last two symbols, representing ",000" and ",000,000", are made up of two separate symbols each. They have a symbol in common, which could be used as a zero in itself.

        Code chart

        Sumero-Akkadian Cuneiform script was added to the Unicode Standard in July, 2006 with the release of version 5.0.

        The Unicode block for Sumero-Akkadian Cuneiform is U+12000‚ÄìU+123FF:

            Letter classification by Gardiner
            Each entry links to the list below.
                vte
            Gardiner's sign list letter classification
            Letter 	Description 	Category (individual hieroglyph articles)
            A 	¬ß Man and his occupations 	Category:Egyptian hieroglyphs: man and his occupations (4) 	
            B 	¬ß Woman and her occupations 	Category:Egyptian hieroglyphs: woman and her occupations (0) 	
            C 	¬ß Anthropomorphic deities 	Category:Egyptian hieroglyphs: anthropomorphic deities (0) 	
            D 	¬ß Parts of the human body 	Category:Egyptian hieroglyphs: parts of the human body (13) 	
            E 	¬ß Mammals 	Category:Egyptian hieroglyphs: mammals (8) 	
            F 	¬ß Parts of mammals 	Category:Egyptian hieroglyphs: parts of mammals (7) 	
            G 	¬ß Birds 	Category:Egyptian hieroglyphs: birds (7) 	
            H 	¬ß Parts of birds 	Category:Egyptian hieroglyphs: parts of birds (1)

            ìÜ§ 	

                L2
                U+131A4

                bee 	

                bee (bjt)

                for bjt (only in "king of lower Egypt" (bjt)) 	This hieroglyphic shows the very important hieroglyphic for bee, that stands also for honey. It is found very often on pharaonic naming-inscriptions-(as the combined term: Nesu-bity), because this hieroglyphic is a symbol for Lower Egypt together with the sedge, the symbol that stands for Upper Egypt, showing the domination of the Pharaohs over Upper Egypt and Lower Egypt.

            See also nswt-bjt
            ìÜ•

                    bil. pr; used extensively in "placenames"-(home of God XXX); placenames for a Pharaoh, etc.
            1. Ideogram, house, estate; 2. bil. pr; 3. Determinative for 'building', 'location'.

            Likely ancestral to Proto-Sinaitic Bet and its descendants.

            In Unicode
            Main article: Egyptian Hieroglyphs (Unicode block)

            Unicode character names follow Gardiner's sign list (padded with zeroes to three digits, i.e. Gardiner "A1" is "EGYPTIAN HIEROGLYPH A001"), with the addition of glyph names in NL001‚ÄìNL020 and NU001‚ÄìNU022, representing the 20 Nomes of Lower Egypt and the 22 Nomes of Upper Egypt, respectively.
